34-15-01AWeather Radar 
Weather Radar with Windshear Detection and  Avoidance System (Predictive) Installed
Not Required by regulation
B 1 0 (O) 
May be inoperative provided:  Interval Installed Required Procedure
1- The aircraft is not dispatched in IFR or at night VFR in areas where weather reports indicate thunderstorms or other
potentially hazardous weather conditions that can be detected by weather radar or may be expected to exist along the route or
if the airspace requires its use
2-Operations in the Intertropical Convergence Zone ITCZ cannot be conducted
Note: The route corresponds to any point along the planned route of flight including possible diversions to alternate airports.
OPERATIONS (O) 
The Flight Crew must be vigilant with regards to aeroplane configuration, altitude and flight path at all times.
To enhance awareness of the above:
• all available aeroplane systems (e.g. autopilot, ILS, FMCS, VSD) must be used;
• Minimum Flight Altitudes must be reviewed; and
• strict adherence to altitude call-outs must be applied.
Flight Crew must additionally review:
• Windshear Avoidance and Precautions (FCOM 1, S.P., Adverse Weather, Windshear),
• Indications that the aeroplane is in windshear (QRH MAN section), and
• The Windshear Escape Maneuver (QRH MAN section).

VOR Systems
Any in excess of one, and not powered by a Standby Bus, may be inoperative provided:  C Interval Installed Required Procedure
2 1 C Interval Installed Required Procedure
1. Both ADF (where required) and DME are operative, and
2. The aeroplane is equipped with alternative equipment authorised, for the route being flown, by the Authority.
MCC and the Commander should consider whether or not the in-flight failure of the remaining VOR System allows safe 
navigation with the remaining operative navigation equipment.
The availability or not of the VOR Systems should be taken into consideration when nominating an aerodrome as an Alternate 
(Enroute, Destination, Takeoff, etc).
Any in excess one (01), and not powered by a Standby Bus, may be inoperative provided approach minimums do not require its 
use. 
NOTE: Note: Both ILS receivers (with valid indication) need to be operative for CAT 2 & 3A approaches. For a CAT 1 
approach, only the ILS (with indication) on the PF side needs to be operative. 
OPERATIONS NOTE 
When dispatched with an inoperative R- ILS, manually tune an ILS frequency on the left Navigation Control Panel (P8) prior to 
takeoff to prevent display of the GPWS INOP light in flight. 
NO AUTOLAND will be displayed in the flight mode annunciation autopilot status on fail operational equipped airplanes. 
For one ILS inoperative, SINGLE CH will be displayed in the flight mode annunciation autopilot status. 34-17

NOTE: If arming LNAV on ground with one radio altimeter inoperative, the flight directors and autopilot should be controlled
 by the FCC on the same side as the valid radio altimeter (i.e., the first flight director and/or autopilot to be engaged
 must be receiving valid radio altitude data).
Note: CAT 2 & 3A approaches require both Radio Altimeters to be operative. For a CAT 1 approach only one RA is required. 
MAINTENANCE (M) 
Do these steps (AMM 34-00-00/901): 
1. Open and collar associated P6-1/P18-1 panel Radio Altimeter circuit breaker to deactivate the inoperative radio altimeter.
NOTE: With one radio altimeter deactivated, the SPEED BRAKE DO NOT ARM light will illuminate on 
 the ground when speed brake handle is moved from the DOWN detent. 
2. For airplanes without FCC Operational Program Software (OPS) 2212-HNP -03B -05 or later installed, re-initialize the Flight
Control Computer (FCC) associated with the inoperative radio altimeter by momentarily opening and then closing
the applicable P6-2/P18-1 panel FCC circuit breaker.
NOTE: Rockwell Collins FCC Operational Program Software (OPS) part numbers are considered to be equivalent  
 to Honeywell FCC OPS part number 2212-H NP-0 3B-05 and later. 
3. For airplanes with PSEU part number 28
5A1600-5 or earlier, refer to MEL Item 32-17. An invalid radio altimeter signal
will generate a dispatchable PSEU fault.
OPERATIONS (O)  
NOTE: For airplanes with -1, -2, or -3 SMYD, an invalid signal from radio altimeter number 1 will result in failure of both 
 stick shakers to self test. 
1. Ensure that weather minimums or operating procedures are not dependent upon its use.
2.With a radio altimeter inoperative, do not use the associated autopilot, associated flight director, or auto throttle
for approach and landing.
NOTE: The FCC engages LNAV when the radio altimeters indicate that airplane  is 50ft above ground level (AGL).  
 Dispatching with an inoperative radio altimeter system may generate an erroneous radio height indication 
 of 50 ft AGL and may cause the LNAV FMA to flash when armed on ground.  
3.For airplanes with FCC Operational Program Software (OPS) 2212-H NP-03B-05 or later installed, if the remaining r
adio altimeter fails:
NOTE: Rockwell Collins FCC Operational Program Software (OPS) part numbers are considered to be equivalent 
 to Honeywell FCC OPS part number 2212-H NP-0 3B-05 and later.  
A.AFDS (both sides) will limit the bank angle to a maximum of 8 degrees in all roll modes.
B.Use of the Autopilot/Flight Director System (AFDS) is at the discretion of the flight crew. 
AFDS may not:
Section 31/ Command sufficient bank angle to execute proper departure and/or approach maneuvers. 
2/ Make enroute course changes within airspace limitations.

34-25 Altitude Alerting System  
A 1 (O) 
May be inoperative provided: 
a. Autopilot with altitude hold, and altitude capture operates normally.
b. Enroute operation, i.e. RVSM, do not require its use.
c.Airplane does not depart from the base  where repair or replacement can be made.
d. Repairs are made within three flight days.
OPERATIONS (O)  
NOTE: An operative altitude alerting system is required for RVSM operations. increase flight crew awareness of altitude, which may 
include the following: 
1. Determine that at least one autopilot is operating normally and that altitude hold and altitude capture are operating normally.
2. Use the autopilot and altitude hold for all operations for which it is appropriate.
3. Cross-check Captain’s and First Officer’s altitude displays upon reaching and departing assigned altitude. Periodically cross-
check altitude indications when maintaining an assigned altitude.
4. Pilot not flying should call out approaching and departing assigned altitudes.
5. Flight deck crew must be aware that the usual alerts for altitude deviations will not occur.

(O) 
May be inoperative provided: 
a. Associated instruments operate normally from isolated sources.

OPERATIONS (O)
Check that associated instruments function properly from isolated sources. 
Note 
1. ILS Category II and III approaches, are NOT authorized.
2. Autoland is NOT authorized.
3. RVSM operations are NOT allowed.
4. PBN Operations (i.e. RNAV 10, RNAV 5, RNAV 2, RNAV 1, RNP 2, RNP 1, RNP APCH) operations are NOT authorized.
5. Ensure that the correct codes for the current RVSM and PBN capabilities are indicated in the ATS FPL fields 10 and 18, taking
into account any malfunctions.
1. Place the IRS mode selector switch for the inoperative IRS to OFF.
2. Use the remaining IRS for both attitude, heading and vertical speed indications.OPERATION
3. Verify that remaining IRS is operating normally by observing attitude and heading flags are out of view on pilot's and
copilot's ADI, HSI, VSI and RDMI.

MAINTENANCE NOTE

operational for dispatch. 
On airplanes with dual FMC’s installed and one FMC inoperative , operating with the FMC Source Select Switch selected to the 
operational FMC (BOTH ON L or BOTH ON R) is required to accomplish all Flight Management Computing tasks. Primary 
means RNP RNAV operations up to a 10 minute duration can be accomplished with a single FMC.

34-37AWindshear Warning and Flight Guidance System 
(Reactive) Alternate Procedures Required
B 1 
May be inoperative provided Operations Procedures are used, as described below.  
OPERATIONS (O) 
The Flight Crew must be vigilant with regards to aeroplane configuration, altitude and flight path at all times.
To enhance awareness of the above:
• all available aeroplane systems (e.g. autopilot, ILS, FMCS, VSD) must be used;
• Minimum Flight Altitudes must be reviewed; and
• strict adherence to altitude call-outs must be applied.
Additionally, the Flight Crew must review:
1. Windshear Avoidance and Precautions (FCOM 1, S.P., Adverse Weather, Windshear),
2. Indications that the aeroplane is in windshear (QRH MAN section), and
3. The Windshear Escape Maneuver (QRH MAN section).
Section 3 (O) 0 Interval Installed Required Procedure3-2 (A/D affected by change)
-the procedure intended to be flown is not identical to the current aeronautical information:
- Do not use the procedures of the out of date navigation database.
-For (Non RNAV/RNP operation): use the procedure intendeded to be flown by manually  tuning
        the radio navigation aids, (VOR, DME, ADF, ILS), 
-For an (RNAV/RNP operation): Conventional (Non-RNAV/RNP) or ANSP assistance are used as
        an alternative to RNAV/RNP procedures which have been amended in the current database cycle,
-the airways are not identical: insert new routings according to the current airways.

MAINTENANCE (M)  
For -600/-700C/-800: 
Check masks in affected PSU and tape door closed (AMM 35-00-00/901). 
For All Models: 
1. For airplanes with bottle passenger oxygen:
A. Tape all oxygen mask compartment doors closed.
B. Pressurize system using an external source connected to the low pressure manifold via the test/vent connection
or by switching the airplane passenger oxygen system on.
C. Check masks in the affected PSU for oxygen flow.
D. Replace valve actuating pins, pack masks in compartment, and tape door closed. Fashion the tape so that a
non-adhesive “handle”, approximately 4 inches long, is left pendant. This “handle” will be used in case of need by
the passenger to strip the securing tape down, thus allowing the door to fall open.
E. Disconnect oxygen source or reset aircraft system by moving PASS OXY switch to the RESET position.
F. Remove tape from all operative oxygen mask compartment doors.
2. For airplanes with chemical passenger oxygen:
A. Verify that related generator has not been expended. Color band will be black if generator has been expended
and generator must be replaced.
B. Tape door closed. Fashion the tape such that a non-adhesive “handle”, approximately 4 inches long, is left
pendant. This “handle” will be used in case of need b y
 the passenger to strip the securing tape down, thu s
allowing the d
oor to fall open

may be inoperative provided: 
a. Valve remains closed except for engine start.

MAINTENANCE (M)  
1. Deactivate the bleed air isolation valve (AMM 36-00-00/901).
A. Set both engine BLEED switches to OFF.
B. Set the APU Bleed Air switch to OFF.
C.Set both PACK  switches to OFF.
D.Open and collar the P6-4 panel circuit breaker AIR CONDITIONING BLEED AIR VALVE ISOLATION.
E. Remove, cap and stow the connector from bleed air isolation valve.
       NOTE: It may be necessary to temporarily remove the air  conditioning duct segment located in front of keel  beam access hole.
F. Manually move the valve to the closed position using the manual override handle.
G. Set the BLEED air and PACK switches as required.
     NOTE: The isolation valve must be manually opened for engine start and then manually closed after the  engines are started.
Personnel should take special care to remain well clear of the engine inlet hazard areas when manually  closing the 
valve after engine start.
2. If the bleed air isolation valve is stuck closed and cannot be opened, do these steps:
A. Set both engine BLEED air switches to OFF.
B. Set the APU BLEED air switch to OFF.
C. Set both PACK switches to OFF.
D. Open and collar the P6-4 panel circuit breaker AIR CONDITIONING BLEED AIR VALVE ISOLATION.
E. Remove, cap and stow the connector from the bleed air isolationvalve.
        NOTE: It may be necessary to temporarily remove the air conditioning duct segment located in front of keel beam access hole

36-04 PNEUMATIC PRESSURE INDICATION SYSTEMS 
2 (O) 
May be inoperative provided Operation procedures are used. as described below.   
OPERATIONS (O) 
1. The Flight Crew normally uses the Pneumatic Pressure Indication System to verify the following during engine starts:
A.Minimum recommended pneumatic pressure for engine start.
B.Closure of the engine start valve if START VALVE OPEN lights are not installed.
2. With an inoperative Pneumatic Pressure Indication System, confirmation of minimum recommended pneumatic
pressure is not required for engine start.
3. For verification of start valve closure:
A. On airplanes with START VALVE OPEN lights installed or equipped with the START VALVE OPEN indication
on the Display Unit (DU), the Flight Crew can verify that the engine start valve has closed by noting that the
START VALVE OPEN lights/indications have extinguished.
B. On airplanes without START VALVE OPEN lights installed, the APU must be used for engine starts. The Flight
Crew should moni
tor the APU EGT and note a pronounced drop at starter cutout.
Section 3OPERATIONS (O)  
For -600/-700 C/-800: 
Performance adjustments. 
Interval Installed Required Procedure
C 0
OPERATIONS (O) 
For engine starts with the START VALVE OPEN light and the associated Pneumatic Pressure Indication System inoperative,  
the APU must be used for engine starts. The Flight Crew should monitor the APU EGT. There will be a pronounced drop in APU  
EGT at starter cutout. NOTE:   Enroute climb penalties are based on single engine operating speeds that approximate maximum lift-to-drag ratio 
speed.  To account for the difference in level off altitude when operating at other speeds, multiply the enroute climb weight 
penalty listed above by the appropriate factor listed in CDL, Enroute Diversion Speed Effects.

Section 3MAINTENANCE (M)
For -600/-700C/-800:
Lock the associated engine bleed air valve in the closed position (AMM 36-00-00/901).
For All Models:
1. Deactivate the leading edge flaps and slats in the retracted position (AMM 27-81-00/201).
2. Deactivate the associated thrust reverser (AMM 78-31-00/201).
3. Gain access to the engine bleed air valv e by opening the appropriate fan cowl panel  (AMM  71-11-02/201)  and
thrust  reverser  (AMM  78-31-00/201).
4. Lock the inoperative engine bleed air valve in the CLOSED position.
A. Turn the override nut to align the position indicator with the CLOSED position.
B. Loosen the lock  screw/knob bolt and push in locking knob to lock valve in closed position.
C. Re-tighten the lock screw/knob bolt.
5. Close fan cowl panel (AMM 71-11-02/201) and thrust reverser (AMM 78-31-00/201).
6. Activate the thrust reverser (AMM 78-31-00/201).
7. Activate the leading edge flaps and slats (AMM 27-81-00/201).
OPERATIONS (O)
NOTE 1:Use of the APU bleed air is limited to 17,000 feet. One air conditioning 
pack will be unusable when dispatching with: (1) the right engine bleed inoperative, (2) the left engine bleed 
inoperative and flight altitude greater than 17,000 feet, or (3) both engine bleeds inoperative.
NOTE 2: When dispatching with a single engine bleed on for takeoff (airplane pressurized), V1(MCG) should be determined
 based on AC packs OFF. Takeoff performance should be based on AC packs AUTO.
1. Do not dispatch into known or forecast icing conditions.
2. Associated engine bleed switch is selected to the OFF position.
3. For left engine bleed inoperative:
A. At altitudes 17,000 feet and below, operate the left pack using the APU bleed air, the right pack using
the right engine bleed and the isolation valve CLOSE .
B. At altitudes above 17,000 feet, operate with the APU bleed air OFF.
1) Limit altitude to FL 250.
2) Operate the left pack using the right engine bleed, the right pack OFF and isolation valve OPEN.
4. For right engine bleed inoperative:
A. Limit altitude to FL 250.
B. Operate the left pack using the left engine bleed, right pack OFF, and isolation valve CLOSE.
NOTE:   At altitudes 17,000 feet and below, increased air flow will occur when flaps are extended
(takeoff and landing) and the APU is used instead of engine bleed to supply bleed air to the operating pack.
Refer to Boeing Operations Manual, NO ENGINE BLEED TAKEOFF AND LANDING PROCEDURE.

A. Turn the override nut to align the position indicator with the CLOSED position.

C. Re-tighten the lock s crew/knob bolt.
5. Close fan cowl panel (AMM 71-11-02/201) and thrust reverser (AMM 78-31-00/201).
6. Activate the thrust reverser (AMM 78-31-00/201).
7. Activate the leading edge flaps and slats (AMM 27-81-00/201).

3  The Commander, in coordination with NCC, will determine if the flight duration is acceptable taking into consideration:
•the passenger loads;
•the flight time;
•the service level (e.g. Business class passengers, etc.);
•any expected delays;
•any relevant information (e.g. the amount of bottled water available, etc.);
Additionally, the Commander shall inform the Cabin Crew that:
•potable water will not be available throughout the flight;
•the water faucets in galleys and lavatories will be inoperative;
•the toilet flush will still be operative but there will be no water coming out during the flush phase
sequence.
Note : If needed, bottled water may be poured during the flush phase sequence to clean the toilet. The Cabin Crew shall:
•ensure that adequate bottled water and hand sanitizer is available for the duration of the flight;
•inform passengers in Arabic, English and any other language, as deemed appropriate about the
unserviceability;
•check on a regular basis during the flight that the toilets, if used, are free of waste;
If the lavatories are not to be used, must be secured closed and placarded INOPERATIVE – DO NOT ENTER. Note : This  
provision is not intended to prohibit inspections by Crew Members.

OPERATIONS (O) 
NOTE: Do not exceed the maximum pressure differential of 6.0 psi. Limit flight altitude to 27,000 feet or lower to maintain a 
cabin altitude of less than 8,000 feet. 
1. Select a landing altitude of 8,000 ft. MSL on the cabin pressure control panel. Cabin altitude will ascend to slightly
less than 8,000 ft. during climb to cruise altitude.
NOTE: Actual landing airport altitude may be selected if flight altitude is limited to 13,000 feet. 
2. Monitor differential pressure indicator during climb to ensure maximum pressure differential of 6.0 psi is not
exceeded.
3.Select actual landing airport altitude after initiating descent. If required to hold during descent, it may be necessary to
increase the landing altitude in accordance with the Differential Pressure Schedule below.
4 .Lower cabin altitudes may be obtained by appropriate selection of flight altitude and cabin/landing altitude 
in accordance with the Differential Pressure Schedule below.

Verify manual mode operates normally (AMM 52-00-00/901).  
1. Verify that the manual mode is operating normally by performing the main deck cargo door manual operation
procedures placarded in the left main wheel well to open and close the cargo door.
2. After opening the cargo door to a stationary position measured five feet vertically above the cargo compartment floor
at STA 470, check for excessive internal cargo door hydraulic system leakage. If the edge of the cargo door skin lowers
more than four inches over a fifteen minute period, dispatch is not allowed.

OPERATIONS (O)
•Engineering will provide the Flight Deck door key to the Commander.
•The Commander will in turn give the key to the PURSER , explaining the use of the key and
reminding the  SCCM to guard the key in a secure location notifying the rest of the Cabin Crew
members.
•Any key holders or notes on the key itself that imply the key is for use with the Flight Deck
door must
 be removed.
•The FLIGHT DECK ACCESS SYSTEM switch must always be in the OFF position (guard extended).
•The FLT DK DOOR, “LOCK FAIL” will be illuminated throughout the whole flight.
CAUTION:  Should the FLIGHT DECK ACCESS SYSTEM switch is set in the NORM position, the door
will be electrically locked and unable to be opened even if the Cabin Crew uses the Flight Deck 
key for the deadbolt.

Section 3• The Flight Deck Crew must ensure that the deadbolt is positioned to the LOCKED KEY OPERABLE position,
and used in this position for the rest of the flight.
•Access to the Flight Deck will be requested via the Interphone and the Flight Deck Door will be
opened, only after positively identifying the area outside the Flight Deck, either by the use of 
the Flight Deck Door Electronic Visual Surveillance System or procedural means if the Flight Deck 
Door Electronic Visual Surveillance System is unserviceable.
• In situations where the Cabin Crew would otherwise use the Emergency Access Code to access
the Flight Deck, the key should be used instead.
• If the Commander has any valid concerns that the security of the passenger compartment is
breached, the deadbolt must be set to the LOCKED KEY INOPERABLE position, and a diversion
 to the nearest suitable airport should be considered.

73-04
73-04-02FUEL FILTER DIFFERENTIAL PRESSURE WARNING SYSTEMS 
-600/-700C/-800
2 1 (M) 
One may be inoperative provided malfunction is verified to be in warning system. 
MAINTENANCE (M) 
For -600/-700 C/-800: 
Verify that the malfunction is in the fuel filter bypass warning system (AMM 73-00-00/901): 
1. If the FILTER BYPASS light illuminates with the engine not operating either with the EEC powered (start switch in
CONT) or EEC not powered (start switch in OFF/AUTO), the fuel filter bypass warning system is faulty. Proceed to step
3 below to replace the fuel filter.
2. If the FILTER BYPASS light does NOT illuminate with the engine not operating, perform the following:
A.If Fuel FILTER BYPASS light was ON prior to engine shutdown, check EEC BITE-RECENT FAULTS for a
"FUEL FILTER SIGNALS DISAGREE" fault message (AMM 73-21-00). If this fault message is present,
proceed to step 3 below to replace the fuel filter.
NOTE: Other EEC fault messages may need to be addressed prior to dispatch. 
B. Ch
eck DEU for fault messages. A CDS MAINT message may indicate a DEU fault that affects the fuel filter bypass
indication. NOTE: A CDS FAULT must be addressed prior to dispatch.
C. If Fuel FILTER BYPASS light is inoperative OFF, do EEC TEST, AMM task 73-21 -00-700 -804-F00.
NOTE: Remaining indication lights in the EEC test should illuminate normally. 
3.Replace fuel filter with a new filter (AMM 73-11-02).
NOTE: Except for ER operations, one flight is permitted prior to filter replacement provided that fuel drained from filter housing 
drain plug is free of visible, gross contamination. 
OPERATION NOTE 
If the remaining FILTER BYPASS light illuminates, assume both engine fuel filters have an impending bypass condition.

A. Open and collar the P6-2 panel circuit breaker ENG 2 ALTN PWR CHAN A or ENG 2 ALTN PWR CHAN B, as
app
ropriate.
Section 3OPERATIONS (O)  
NOTE: Maximum rated thrust may be reached at a reduced thrust lever position. 
1. Position both EEC Mode switches to ALTN.
2. For 18K through 24K thrust ratings, use full rated takeoff thrust (derated and/or assumed temperature method
reduced thrust takeoffs are not allowed).
3. For 26K or 27K thrust ratings takeoff thrust derates utilizing thrust levels down to and including 24K are permissible only
for the -700 (assumed temperature method reduced thrust takeoffs are not allowed).
4. For -700’s with 27k thrust rating: (1) 26K or 24K thrust derate must be used for takeoff when gross weight is less than
130,000 lb (58,967 kg), (2) 24K thrust derate must be used for takeoff when gross weight is less than 125,000 lb (56,699
kg).
5. For -700’s with 26K thrust rating: 24K thrust derate must be used for takeoff when takeoff weight is less than 125,000
lb (56,699 kg).
6. For takeoff at the 26K or 27K thrust levels: Do not use FMC-computed V-speeds or takeoff thrust N1 values. Refer to
AFM-DPI for appropriate takeoff performance adjustments, V-speeds and takeoff thrust N1 values (use manual takeof f
thrust setting procedures).
Interval Installed Required ProcedureNOTE 1:Dispatch is not allowed with ENGINE CONTROL light(s) illuminated or inoperative. 
NOTE 2:Operation with Electronic Engine Controls (EEC’s) in Alternate (ALTN) mode is allowed

Section 3Airplanes not equipped with R913/R914 Power Sense relays for the ignition system. Right Ignition System(s), 
connect the LEFT igniter to AC Standby Bus (AMM 74-00-00/901): 
1. Open applicable P18-2/P6-2 Panel circuit breakers:
A Engine No. 1 - ENGINE 1 IGNITION RIGHT and ENGINE 1 
IGNITION LEFT 
B. Engine No. 2 - ENGINE 2 IGNITION RIGHT and ENGINE 2
IGNITION LEFT
2. Without automatic ignition:
Verify that the start levers are in the CUTOFF position and ENGINE START switch is in the OFF position.
3.Open fan cowl on the associated engine.
WARNING:  MAKE SURE THE IGNITION EXCITERS ARE DE-ENERGIZED BEFORE WORKING ON THE IGNITION 
SYSTEM. WAIT FOR A MINIMUM OF FIVE MINUTES TO RELEASE THE HIGH VOLTAGE FROM IGNITION EXCITER.  
5. Disconnect LEFT/RIGHT power supply cables from the LEFT/RIGHT ignition exciter.
6. Connect cables as follows:
A. LEFT power supply cable to RIGHT exciter.
B. RIGHT power supply cable to LEFT exciter.
7. Close the circuit breakers opened in Step 1.
8. Perform Audible Test of Ignition System - EEC BITE.
9. Close fan cowl on the associated engine.

77-05
77-05-02 VIBRATION INDICATING SYSTEMS 
-600/-700C/-800
1 
NOTE1: The MEL item refers to the Vibration Indicating System and not to the Vibration Indicator Sensors.
Company aircraft are equipped with two Vibration Indicating Systems (one per engine).
If the aircraft is dispatched with erroneous or invalid vibration indications for one engine, disregard
the indications and do not proceed to the QRH Non-Normal Checklist "Engine High Vibration" should
a value higher than 4 units is displayed.
A relief according to this MEL item if both engine vibration indicators are operative, is not required.
At least one engine vibration indicator in the Flight Deck should be operative.
NOTE 2 :Operating the airplane with one number 1 bearing vibration sensor deactivated per AMM 77-31-05/201 meets 
all design flight deck engine vibration Indication (refer to Boeing Service Letter 737-SL-77-016), and therefore MEL 
relief is not required.

MAINTENANCE (M)  
For -600/-700C/-800:      For dispatch, perform the following verification steps once each flight day(AMM 79-00-00/901): 
1.Verify the malfunction is in the bypass warning system:
A.Verify presence of fault code 79-n112x on the FMC CDU (AMM 73-21-00/501).
B.If fault code 79-n112x is not present, access the CDU INPUT MONITORING / OIL FILTER screen on the FMC CDU
and verify FILTER BYPASS state is "CLOGGED", which corresponds to the following FILTER INPUTS displayed
on the FMC CDU: Switch 1 (Channels A and B) OPEN, Switch 2 (Channels A and B) CLOSED.
2.Inspect all three Magnetic Chip Detectors for contaminants (AMM 79-00-00/601).
3.Verify the oil supply filter pop-out indicator is not extended (AMM 79-00-00/601).
4.If Magnetic Chip Detectors inspection reveals no contaminants and oil supply filter pop-out indicator is not extended,
then the malfunction is in the warning system.

A.Prior to selecting ENGINE START switch to GRD position note the duct pressure.

E.Set each engine start lever in the CUTOFF position.

MISCELLANEOUS - NEF REV 1 
DEF P 01 
INTRODUCTION
4.1 NEF P ROGRAM
4.1.1 Preamble 
Nonessential Equipment and Furnishing (NEF) are those items installed on the aircraft as part of the original 
certification, Supplemental Type Certificate (STC), Minor Design Change (DOA), or other form of alteration 
that have no effect on the safe operation off light and would not be required by the applicable Certification 
Rules or Operational Rules. They are those items that if inoperative, damaged, or missing, have no effect on 
the aircraft’s ability to be operated safely under all operational conditions. NEF items may be instal
led in 
areas including, but not limited to the: 
•passenger compartment,
• flight deck area,
NEF ti em s  r ue l . 
• service areas,
• cargo areas,
• lavatories, and
• galley areas.
NEF items are not instrument and equipment items already identified in the MEL or CDL. They do not include 
instrument and equipment items that are functionally required to meet the certification rule or for compliance with 
any operational rule. 
Before deferring an item in accordance with the NEF Program, it has to be assured that the source of the 
damage/condition has been identified and appropriately addressed. 
By definition, NEF items do not, and should not, affect the safe operation of an aircraft. 
4.1.2 Responsibility 
The NEF Program is developed by Air Algerie Engineering, and it is provided to Flight Operations for 
inclusion in the NEF Manual. 
Through the NEF Program development process, NEF items are identified, the NEF list is defined, 
maintained and revised, and Maintenance and/or Operations procedures are defined (as applicable). 
All amendments/revisions to the NEF are first internally approved by Flight Ops, Engineering & Maintenance 
and Quality Assurance. By approving the proposed amendments/revisions it is agreed by all parties that the 
amendments/revisions fulfil the criteria specified per 4.1.3.2 Determination of NEF Items . 
4.1.3 Air Algerie NEF Program 
Air algerie NEF Program uses the deferral authority granted in the MEL as a basis for developing a Company 
specific program that, provides: 
• Relief for inoperative, damaged or missing non-essential items, and
• Maintenance and Operations procedures, as applicable and necessary, for the safe operation of the
aircraft.
Any portion of the NEF Program that has reference to maintenance, complies with standard maintenance 
practices and/or applicable approved data. 
Air Algerie NEF Program does not provide for deferral of items within serviceable limits identified in the 
Aircraft Maintenance Manual (AMM) or Air Algerie Approved Maintenance Program such as wear limits, 
fuel/hydraulic leak rates, oil consumption, etc . NEF 
B737-6 00/- 700C/-  
800/800BCF  NOV 27 2023  
DEFINITION
Section 4

===PAGE457===
MISCELLANEOUS - NEF REV 1 
DEF P 02 
Cosmetic items that are fully serviceable but cosmetically damaged may be deferred under this program. 
Although, the NEF program is listed under Chapter 25 of the MEL, it addresses items that fall under other 
ATA chapters. 
The Air Algerie NEF Program encompasses: 
4.1.3.2 Determination of NEF Items 
• The NEF list,
• A process for evaluating an item to be included in the NEF List
• Repair and/or replacement policy and procedures.
4.1.3.1  NEF List 
In order to identify items that may be included in the NEF List, Air Algerie NEF Program follows the 
procedure described in 4.1.3.2 . 
As new NEF items are identified they are added to the NEF list. 
The NEF List is divided into 8 Parts: 
Part Description 
A 
B Galley 
C Flight Deck 
D Lavatories 
E Service Bays 
F Passenger Seats 
G Cargo Compartment 
H Placards & Miscellaneous 
4.1.3.2 Detremination of NEF Items 
All items related to the airworthiness, or required for the safe operation of the aircraft are automatically 
required to be operative. However, certain equipment may be installed for convenience and therefore do not 
affect the airworthiness or operation of the aircraft when inoperative. 
Air Algerie has established a decision-making process for items that are not listed or addressed in the MEL 
to determine if they are related to airworthiness and/or required for sa fe operation. 
NEF items can be proposed by anyone. Proposals can be made to the engineering or Operations 
department who will initiate the evaluation process. 
Engineering, Maintenance, and Operations will work together, establishing communication channels, to 
determine NEF item suitability. MEL/NEF amendments have to be agreed by both Operations and 
Engineering, therefore neither one can add an NEF item unilaterally. 
When evaluating an item for NEF List inclusion, any Maintenance (M), or Operations (O) procedures are first 
to be determined and defined, along with the proposed failure conditions (i.e. missing, loose, damaged, 
worn/deteriorated, inoperative, etc). The proposal is then considered against the following criteria: NEF 
B737-6 00/- 700C/-  
800/800BCF  NOV 27 2023 
DEFINITION
Section 4Cabine Interior  

===PAGE458===
MISCELLANEOUS - NEF REV 1 
DEF P 03 
If item is, 
1 Functionally required for Operational Rules in which the aircraft is  operated;  
2. Required due to a secondary safety related  function;
3. Beyond its serviceable  limits;
Note:  Items may have associated fire retardant/blocking requirements that must be co nsidered before
approving as an NEF item.
Additionally, if the item and its proposed failure condition:  
4. Adversely affects Standard Operating Procedures related to ground personnel, and/or crew
members;
5. Affects the safety of passengers, crew, or service personnel under all operational  conditions;
6. Affects the safety of passengers, crew, or service personnel and/or cause damage to the aircraft,
should a subsequent failure  occur;
7. Creates the potential for fire/smoke or other hazardous  conditions;
8. Results in an adverse effect on other required systems or  components;
9. Results in a negative impact on emergency or abnormal  procedures;
10. Creates additional workload for the crew at critical times of flight or during flight  preparation;
11. Results in a flight safe ty concern or adverse effect on the safe conduct of flight under all operational
conditions;
12. Affects an equivalent level of safety;
Note:  This consideration process is accomplished for the inoperative, damaged, or missing item at its
face value, and also for any underlying cause of discrepancy.
if any of the answers to the above questions is positive (yes) then the item can not be included in the NEF List.  
In the development stage of NEF proposals these can be re-defined and re-evaluated as required until the 
criteria are satisfied. It should also be noted, that subcomponents of MEL, CDL, or MEL items are not 
permitted to be NEF items. 
If inclusion of any item is in question, the appropriate design organisation will first be consulted to ver ify that 
an item can be placed on the NEF list.  
4.1.3.3  Repair and/or Replacement  Policy  
Inoperative N EF items will be recorded in the Aircraft Technical Logbook in the same manner as MEL items.  
The repair interval for NEF items is D (120 days) and may be extend ed if condition of defect is still within 
requirements of NEF program. Refer to 4.1.3.7 – NEF Rectification Interval Extensions . 
Each inoperative item shall be placarded, as applicable, to inform and remind the crewmembers and 
maintenance personnel of the equipment condition.  
4.1.3.4  NEF Definitions  
For NEF definition refer to MEL Definitions (28). NEF

Legend:

applicable. Up to four levels can be shown here and are repeated from the table of contents. It is
usually the number on the bottom line that will be used in the NEF release. Tail numbers are used
to distinguish data peculiar to one or more, but not all of the aeroplanes. Where data applies to all
aeroplanes listed in the OPS Spec, no reference is made to individual aeroplanes.

7. Location and instructions for placard, “-” if not applicable.
8. NEF Remarks and Exceptions. In this area statement(s) may be included either restricting or
permitting operations with specific conditions and/or limitations for such operations.
Appropriate .air algerie notes may or may not be shown.
9. A “Air Algerie note” provides information giving further guidance or clarification.
10. Description of MAINTENANCE (M) or OPERATIONS (O) Procedure(s) as evaluated and defined
by Engineering and/or Flight Operations.
